  Therefore, none of the above choices are likely causes of obstructive sleep apnea.

  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg

  Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin are statins that can lower LDL, but they do not have a significant effect on TG levels.
  Fenofibrate can reduce TG and increase HDL levels.
  Therefore, Fenofibrate is the preferred medication for this patient.

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Thought: 
  The third ventricle is a cavity located in the brain, between the right and left thalamus.
  The floor of the third ventricle contains several structures, including the optic stalk, which connects the hypothalamus to the optic nerve, the infundibulum, which connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland, and the mammillary bodies, which are located on the posterior wall of the hypothalamus.
  The third nerve is not located on the floor of the third ventricle, but rather exits the brainstem and enters the cavernous sinus where it supplies muscles of the eye.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Third nerve.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought: 
  The floor of third ventricle is a thin median membrane.
  It separates the third ventricle from the lower parts of the brain.
  The optic stalk, infundibulum and mammillary body are structures that are present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  The third nerve is not present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Third nerve.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 2:
Thought:
The floor of the third ventricle lies at its bottom and is formed by various structures that are present above it. It contains:

- The optic chiasm, which lies anterior to the floor of third ventricle.
- The infundibulum, which is a funnel-shaped protrusion that arises from the floor of the hypothalamus and extends downwards to become continuous with the pituitary gland.
- The mammillary bodies, which are a pair of small, round structures that bulge out of the posterior wall of the hypothalamus.
- The third nerve, which is a cranial nerve that arises from the midbrain and supplies the muscles of the eyeball.

Therefore, the structure that is not present on the floor of third ventricle is the optic stalk, which lies anterior to the floor of third ventricle and connects the optic vesicle to the forebrain.

  D: Child less than 2 years

  Cystic fibrosis patients are vulnerable to pneumococcal disease.
  Sickle cell anemia patients are also vulnerable to pneumococcal disease.
  Recurrent rhinitis and sinusitis are not caused by Streptococcus pneumoniae.
  PPV-23 is not recommended for children less than 2 years of age.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Cystic fibrosis patient.

  Children less than 2 years are vaccinated with a different type of pneumonia vaccine (PCV13).

Question: Gutta Percha can effectively be sterilized by?

  B: Chemical solutions

  Issuing a death certificate is mandatory before embalming a dead body.
  Therefore, embalming without issuing a death certificate is illegal and punishable by law in India.
  Section 297 of the Indian Penal Code (IPC) deals with the punishment for tresspassing on burial places and offering indignity to human remains.
  Section 299 of the IPC deals with the punishment for culpable homicide not amounting to murder.
  Section 498 of the IPC deals with the punishment for subjecting a married woman to cruelty.
  Section 201 of the IPC deals with the punishment for causing disappearance of evidence of an offence.
  Embalming without issuing a death certificate does not fall under any of the above sections.

  Section 299 of the IPC is about culpable homicide not amounting to murder.
  Section 498 of the IPC deals with the punishment for cruelty towards a woman by her husband or relative of the husband.
  Section 201 of the IPC is about causing disappearance of evidence of an offense.

  Supporting cusps assist the opposing teeth in bearing the occlusal load.
  Holding cusps are not a known type of cusps in dentistry.
  Balancing cusps are the cusps that help to maintain vertical dimension and provide stability to the mandible.

  The oral cavity drains into the cervical lymph nodes, which are the regional lymph nodes for the head and neck.
  Lymphatic spread is the most common route of metastasis in oral cancer, followed by direct extension, and then blood vessel spread.
  Aspiration of tumor cells can occur, but it is not a common route of metastasis.
  Therefore, the answer is B: Lymphatics.
Action: Answer("B")

Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Thought: 
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical technique used in periodontal surgery.
  Roots denuded for 6 years means that the tooth has been missing gums for 6 years.
  The principle of lateral sliding flap is to reflect the flap laterally and to gain access to the root.
  Since the roots have been denuded for 6 years, there will be no PDL fibres attached to it.
  Option C is incorrect because lateral sliding flap does not involve epithelium.
  Option D is also incorrect because there will be no adaption to remaining fibres since roots are denuded.
  Therefore, the correct answer is B: PDL fibres attached to dentin.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:

In teeth with roots denuded for 6 years, the periodontal ligament (PDL) fibers that were attached to the cementum may have been destroyed, leading to attachment to dentin or bone.
An epithelial layer may have formed over the denuded roots.
Therefore, the answer is C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface.

  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8

  The modified Bishop Score parameters and their respective points are:

    3. Station - Score 0-2
    4. Cervical consistency - Score 0-2
    5. Cervical position - Score 0-2
    
  In this case:
    Dilation is 1 cm; Score 0
    Effacement is 30%; Score 0
    Station is -1; Score 1
    Cervical consistency is soft; Score 2
    Cervical position is posterior; Score 0
    
  Adding the scores: 0+0+1+2+0 = 3
  Therefore, the modified bishop score for this lady is 3.

Topic: Dental
Question: Multi constricted apical constriction is seen in which type of Dummers classification
Choices:
  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Thought:
  Dummer's classification is a classification system used to categorize the anatomy of the root canal system.
  Multi-constricted apical constriction is a condition in which there are multiple narrow areas at the end of the root canal.
  According to Dummer's classification, Type 1 canals have a single, straight canal from the pulp chamber to the apex.
  Type 2 canals have a single, straight canal from the pulp chamber to the mid-root, with one or more branches in the apical third.
  Type 3 canals have multiple, separate canals that join together in the apical third.
  Type 4 canals have multiple, separate canals that do not join together.
  Based on this information, multi-constricted apical constriction is most likely seen in Type 3 canals.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Dummer's classification is used to classify root canals.
  Multi constricted apical constriction means that the apical constriction is constricted in more than one area.
  Type 1 refers to a root canal that has one main canal from the orifice to the apex.
  Type 2 refers to a root canal that has one main canal from the orifice to the middle third of the root and then divides into two separate canals.
  Type 3 refers to a root canal that has one main canal from the orifice to the apex and also has a smaller lateral canal.
  Type 4 refers to a root canal that has multiple canals that join into one main canal.
  Since multi constricted apical constriction is seen in more than one area, it is most likely present in a root canal that has multiple canals that join into one main canal.
  Therefore, the answer is D: Type 4.
Action: Answer("D")

Topic: Dental
Question: Sealants are effective in
Choices:
  A: Initial caries
  B: Secondary caries
  C: Recurrent caries
  D: Rampant caries
Response 0:
Thought:
  Sealants are thin coatings placed over the chewing surfaces of the teeth, especially molars and premolars to protect them from tooth decay.
  Initial caries refers to the very early stage of tooth decay when a white spot appears on the tooth surface.
  Secondary caries refers to tooth decay that occurs adjacent to a pre-existing restoration such as fillings or crowns.
  Recurrent caries refers to tooth decay that occurs adjacent to the margin of an existing filling or crown.
  Rampant caries refers to a particularly aggressive type of tooth decay that affects multiple teeth at once.
  Therefore, sealants are most effective in preventing initial caries.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Sealants are applied to the grooves and pits of the molar teeth to create a smooth surface.
  The sealant material fills in the grooves and pits and "seals" them so that food particles and bacteria cannot get in.
  Sealants are effective in preventing cavities (tooth decay) by creating a physical barrier to protect the tooth.
  Caries is another term for tooth decay.
  Initial caries means the very early stage of tooth decay.
  Secondary caries refers to new decay that forms around a filling.
  Recurrent caries means decay that forms around the edges of a filling.
  Rampant caries is a severe type of tooth decay that affects multiple teeth.
  Since sealants protect against tooth decay, the best option is initial caries, which is the earliest stage of tooth decay. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:

Topic: Pathology
Question: Which of the following may be a feature of acromegaty?
Choices:
  A: Large tongue
  B: Micrognathia
  C: Hypoglycemia
  D: Crowded teeth
Response 0:
Thought: 
  Acromegaly is a disorder of growth hormone excess resulting in enlargement of the hands, feet and head. It can also have systemic effects including the following:
    - Large tongue
    - Prognathism (protruding jaw)
    - Malocclusion, teeth crowding
  Hypoglycemia is not a feature of acromegaly. In fact, hyperglycemia or impaired glucose tolerance may occur in some patients with acromegaly.
  Micrognathia is a condition where the jaw is undersized, and is usually associated with genetic syndromes such as Pierre Robin syndrome or Treacher Collins syndrome.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Acromegaly is a hormonal disorder that results from an excess of growth hormone (GH) after the growth plates have closed.
  The excess GH activity causes the enlargement of bones, cartilage, and other tissues, resulting in characteristic features such as large hands and feet, coarsened facial features, and prognathism.
  Therefore, some of the features of acromegaly involve the enlargement of the tongue, jaw, and teeth, and not their reduction.
  Additionally, acromegaly can cause insulin resistance and hyperglycemia, rather than hypoglycemia.
Action: Answer("A")

Thought:
  Acromegaly is a condition that results from excess growth hormone (GH) production.
  GH stimulates the growth of bones and other tissues in the body.
  In acromegaly, GH production remains high in adults long after normal growth has stopped.
  Some of the common features of acromegaly include an enlarged jaw (prognathism), large tongue, crowding of teeth, and prominent brow and forehead.
  Hypoglycemia is not a feature of acromegaly.

Question: Which of the following is rapid source of energy by resynthesizing ATP for exercising muscles is?
Choices:
  A: Glycolysis
  B: Glycogenolysis
  C: TCA cycle
  D: Phosphocreatine
Response 0:
Thought:
  Glycolysis is the metabolic pathway that converts glucose into pyruvate fueling ATP production.
  Glycogenolysis is the breakdown of glycogen to glucose fueling ATP production.
  TCA cycle is a series of chemical reactions used by organisms to release stored energy through the oxidation of acetyl-CoA derived from carbohydrates, fats, and proteins into carbon dioxide and chemical energy in the form of ATP.
  Phosphocreatine is a high-energy molecule that can be rapidly broken down to create ATP, which can fuel muscle contractions.
  Phosphocreatine system is the short-term, high-intensity energy system used for activities such as sprinting, jumping, and weightlifting. 
  Therefore, the rapid source of energy by resynthesizing ATP for exercising muscles is Phosphocreatine.

Question: A 9 year old boy presenting with lytic lesion on midshaft tibia. On HPE, there are grooved nuclei, giant cells eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation. Xray is as shown below. What is the likely diagnosis?
Choices:
  A: Langerhans cell histiocytosis
  B: Giant cell tumor
  C: Chondroblastoma
  D: Osteoid osteoma
Response 0:
Thought:
  In a 9 year old boy with a lytic lesion on the midshaft tibia, the most likely diagnosis is a benign bone tumor.
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis usually presents with a solitary bone lesion in children and is characterized by proliferation of Langerhans cells.
  Giant cell tumor is a benign tumor which is characterized by proliferation of osteoclast-like multinucleated giant cells.
  Chondroblastoma usually presents as an epiphyseal lesion of long bones.
  Osteoid osteoma usually presents with a painful lesion in the cortex of long bones.
  The HPE findings of grooved nuclei, giant cells, and eosinophilic cytoplasm are characteristic of a giant cell tumor.
  The Xray shows a lytic lesion with cortical breach which is also characteristic of a giant cell tumor.
  Therefore, the likely diagnosis is B: Giant cell tumor.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Langerhans cell histiocytosis (LCH) is a rare disease that occurs most commonly in children.
  Giant cell tumor (GCT) is a benign tumor usually occurring in the epiphysis of long bones.
  Chondroblastoma is a rare benign neoplasm that arises in the epiphysis or apophysis of a long bone.
  Osteoid osteoma is a benign tumor usually occurring in the cortex of long bones.
  The patient is a 9 year old boy with a lytic lesion on the midshaft of his tibia, and on HPE, there are grooved nuclei, giant cells eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation.
  This is suggestive of Langerhans cell histiocytosis.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Thought: 
  Lytic lesion on midshaft tibia in a 9-year-old boy can be due to various causes.
  Grooved nuclei, giant cells eosinophilic cytoplasm and fibroblastic proliferation suggest a benign bone tumor.

Question: In lead poisoning, there is an inhibition of some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway. This is reflected by the accumulation of what substance in blood?
Choices:
  A: Uroporphyrinogen III
  B: Ferrochelatase
  C: Porphob I inogen
  D: Delta amino levulinic acid
Response 0:
Thought:
  In lead poisoning, there is an inhibition of some enzymes of heme biosynthetic pathway.
  This leads to the accumulation of intermediates in the pathway.
  Uroporphyrinogen III synthase is inhibited by lead in the pathway and this leads to the accumulation of uroporphyrinogen III.
  Therefore, the answer is A: Uroporphyrinogen III.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Heme is an important component of hemoglobin in the blood.
  Lead poisoning inhibits some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  Porphyrin is a molecule that forms the basis for heme biosynthesis.
  Accumulation of porphyrin intermediates can occur due to the inhibition of these enzymes.
  The accumulation of which substance in the blood reflects such an inhibition?
  The intermediate between porphyrin and heme is called porphobilinogen (PBG).
  Therefore, the answer is C: Porphobinogen.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Thought:
  Lead poisoning inhibits some of the enzymes of the heme biosynthetic pathway.
  The accumulation of what substance in blood reflects this inhibition?
  The heme biosynthetic pathway is as follows: succinyl coA + glycine -> delta-aminolevulinic acid -> porphobilinogen -> uroporphyrinogen III -> coproporphyrinogen III -> protoporphyrin IX -> heme.
  The enzyme inhibited in lead poisoning is ferrochelatase, which catalyzes the insertion of iron into protoporphyrin IX to form heme. 
  Therefore, the substance that will accumulate in lead poisoning due to the inhibition of ferrochelatase is protoporphyrin IX.
  The answer is None of the above.
Action: Answer("None of the above")

Thought:

Topic: Social & Preventive Medicine
Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Thought:
- Systematic Random Sampling is selecting every kth individual from a list of population. It ensures the randomness of the process but does not take into account factors that can affect the results.
- Simple Random Sampling is selecting individuals without any prior categorization. This method is also random but again does not consider factors that can affect the results.
- Stratified Random Sampling involves categorizing the population based on specific factors which can affect the results and then selecting individuals from each category. This method is often used for ensuring representation of different subgroups in the population.
- Cluster Sampling is used when it is hard or impossible to sample individuals one by one. Instead, groups (clusters) are selected and all individuals within the group are included in the sample. 

Given the question, the method that is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results is Stratified Random Sampling. Hence, the answer is C: Stratified random sampling. 

Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Systematic random sampling is used when all members of the population are known and the researcher wants to select a portion of the members in an ordered way.
  Simple random sampling is a method of selecting a sample from a larger population without any pre-set pattern or order.
  Stratified random sampling divides the population into subgroups and then randomly selects samples from each subgroup.
  Cluster sampling involves dividing the population into groups, or clusters, and randomly selecting entire clusters to be part of the sample.
  The question is asking about selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results.
  Stratified random sampling seems to be the best choice since it involves dividing the population into subgroups based on potential factors that may affect the results.
Action: Answer("C")
